# Remove menu render from Backend | NextJS | Able Pro

NEXT (TS)

NEXT (JS)

In the Able Pro React admin, a few **dashboard menus (i.e. Default, Analytics, Components)** load from our mock API ([GitHub repository](https://github.com/phoenixcoded20/mock-data-api-nextjs)
). If you want to remove it from your admin panel, follow the steps below and remove/edit the suggested line of code.

1.  **Delete the menu-items file** `dashboard.tsx` \[`src/menu-items/dashboard.jsx`\]
    
2.  **Open file** `src/layout/DashboardLayout/Drawer/DrawerContent/Navigation/index.tsx` **and edit the line of code.**
    

**From:**

src/layout/DashboardLayout/Drawer/DrawerContent/Navigation/index.tsx

Copy

    import { Fragment, useLayoutEffect, useState } from 'react';
    ...
    import menuItem from 'menu-items';
    import { useGetMenu, useGetMenuMaster } from 'api/menu';

**To:**

src/layout/DashboardLayout/Drawer/DrawerContent/Navigation/index.tsx

Copy

    import { Fragment, useState } from 'react';
    ...
    import menuItems from 'menu-items';
    import { useGetMenuMaster } from 'api/menu';

1.  **Open file** `src/layout/DashboardLayout/Drawer/DrawerContent/Navigation/index.tsx` **and remove the line of code.**
    

src/layout/DashboardLayout/Drawer/DrawerContent/Navigation/index.tsx

Copy

    import { MenuFromAPI } from 'menu-items/dashboard';
    
    
    function isFound(arr: any, str: string) {
      return arr.items.some((element: any) => {
    	if (element.id === str) {
    	  return true;
    	}
    	return false;
      });
    }
    	
    export default function Navigation() {
    	...		
    	const { menuLoading } = useGetMenu();		
    	...		
    	const [menuItems, setMenuItems] = useState<{ items: NavItemType[] }>({ items: [] });
    
    	let dashboardMenu = MenuFromAPI();
    
    	useLayoutEffect(() => {
    		if (menuLoading && !isFound(menuItem, 'group-dashboard-loading')) {
    		  menuItem.items.splice(0, 0, dashboardMenu);
    		  setMenuItems({ items: [...menuItem.items] });
    		} else if (!menuLoading && dashboardMenu?.id !== undefined && !isFound(menuItem, 'group-dashboard')) {
    		  menuItem.items.splice(0, 1, dashboardMenu);
    		  setMenuItems({ items: [...menuItem.items] });
    		} else {
    		  setMenuItems({ items: [...menuItem.items] });
    		}
    	// eslint-disable-next-line
    	}, [menuLoading]);
    }

1.  **Open file** `src\api\menu.ts` **and edit the line of code.**
    

**From:**

src/api/menu.ts

Copy

    import { MenuProps, NavItemType } from 'types/menu';

**To:**

src/api/menu.ts

Copy

    import { MenuProps } from 'types/menu';

1.  **Open the file** `src\api\menu.ts` **and remove the code below.**
    

src/api/menu.ts

Copy

    import { fetcher } from 'utils/axios';
    	
    export const endpoints = {
      ...
      dashboard: '/dashboard' // server URL
    };
    	
    export function useGetMenu() {
      const { data, isLoading, error, isValidating } = useSWR(endpoints.key + endpoints.dashboard, fetcher, {
    	revalidateIfStale: false,
    	revalidateOnFocus: false,
    	revalidateOnReconnect: false
      });
    
      const memoizedValue = useMemo(
    	() => ({
    	  menu: data?.dashboard as NavItemType,
    	  menuLoading: isLoading,
    	  menuError: error,
    	  menuValidating: isValidating,
    	  menuEmpty: !isLoading && !data?.length
    	}),
    	[data, error, isLoading, isValidating]
      );
    
      return memoizedValue;
    }

In the Able Pro React admin, a few **dashboard menus (i.e. Default, Analytics, Components)** load from our mock API ([GitHub repository](https://github.com/phoenixcoded20/mock-data-api-nextjs)
). If you want to remove it from your admin panel, follow the steps below and remove/edit the suggested line of code.

1.  **Delete menu-items file** `dashboard.jsx` \[`src/menu-items/dashboard.jsx`\]
    
2.  **Open file** `src/layout/DashboardLayout/Drawer/DrawerContent/Navigation/index.jsx` **and edit the below line of code.**
    

**From:**

src/layout/DashboardLayout/Drawer/DrawerContent/Navigation/index.jsx

Copy

    import { Fragment, useLayoutEffect, useState } from 'react';
    ...
    import menuItem from 'menu-items';
    import { useGetMenu, useGetMenuMaster } from 'api/menu';

**To:**

src/layout/DashboardLayout/Drawer/DrawerContent/Navigation/index.jsx

Copy

    import { Fragment, useState } from 'react';
    ...
    import menuItems from 'menu-items';
    import { useGetMenuMaster } from 'api/menu';

1.  **Open file** `src/layout/DashboardLayout/Drawer/DrawerContent/Navigation/index.jsx` **and remove the below line of code.**
    

src/layout/DashboardLayout/Drawer/DrawerContent/Navigation/index.jsx

Copy

    import { MenuFromAPI } from 'menu-items/dashboard';
    
    function isFound(arr, str) {
      return arr.items.some((element) => {
        if (element.id === str) {
          return true;
        }
        return false;
      });
    }
    	
    export default function Navigation() {
    	...		
    	const { menuLoading } = useGetMenu();		
    	...		
    	const [menuItems, setMenuItems] = useState({ items: [] });
    
    	const dashboardMenu = MenuFromAPI();
    
    	useLayoutEffect(() => {
    		if (menuLoading && !isFound(menuItem, 'group-dashboard-loading')) {
    		  menuItem.items.splice(0, 0, dashboardMenu);
    		  setMenuItems({ items: [...menuItem.items] });
    		} else if (!menuLoading && dashboardMenu?.id !== undefined && !isFound(menuItem, 'group-dashboard')) {
    		  menuItem.items.splice(0, 1, dashboardMenu);
    		  setMenuItems({ items: [...menuItem.items] });
    		} else {
    		  setMenuItems({ items: [...menuItem.items] });
    		}
    	// eslint-disable-next-line
    	}, [menuLoading]);
    }

1.  **Open the file** `src\api\menu.js` **and remove the code below.**
    

src/api/menu.js

Copy

    import { fetcher } from 'utils/axios';
    	
    export const endpoints = {
      ...
      dashboard: '/dashboard' // server URL
    };
    	
    export function useGetMenu() {
      const { data, isLoading, error, isValidating } = useSWR(endpoints.key + endpoints.dashboard, fetcher, {
    	revalidateIfStale: false,
    	revalidateOnFocus: false,
    	revalidateOnReconnect: false
      });
    
      const memoizedValue = useMemo(
    	() => ({
    	  menu: data?.dashboard,
    	  menuLoading: isLoading,
    	  menuError: error,
    	  menuValidating: isValidating,
    	  menuEmpty: !isLoading && !data?.length
    	}),
    	[data, error, isLoading, isValidating]
      );
    
      return memoizedValue;
    }

# Render Menu from the backend | NextJS | Able Pro

Able Pro is already rendering the menu from the backend. The dashboard menus (Default, Analytics) are rendered via the back end.

You can check the Fack backend API here that we used to render the menu:

[![Logo](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fgithub.com%2Ffluidicon.png&width=20&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9e53c2a0&sv=2)GitHub - phoenixcoded20/mock-data-api-nextjsGitHub](https://github.com/phoenixcoded20/mock-data-api-nextjs)

NEXT (TS)

NEXT (JS)

To add a menu from the backend, you can follow the steps below:

1.  Open the file `**menu.ts**` _(src/api/menu.ts)_, and edit the API URL in the **useGetMenu** function
    

src/api/menu.ts

Copy

    const endpoints = {
      key: 'api/menu',
      dashboard: '/dashboard' // server URL
    };
    
    export function useGetMenu() {
      const { data, isLoading, error, isValidating } = useSWR(endpoints.key + endpoints.dashboard, fetcher, {
        revalidateIfStale: false,
        revalidateOnFocus: false,
        revalidateOnReconnect: false
      });
    
      const memoizedValue = useMemo(() => {
        let updatedMenu = data?.dashboard;
    
        if (updatedMenu && Array.isArray(updatedMenu.children) && updatedMenu.children.length > 0) {
          updatedMenu = {
            ...updatedMenu,
            children: updatedMenu.children.map((group: NavItemType) => {
              if (Array.isArray(group.children)) {
                return {
                  ...group,
                  children: [...group.children, staticMenuItem]
                };
              }
              return group;
            })
          };
        }
    
        return {
          menu: updatedMenu as NavItemType,
          menuLoading: isLoading,
          menuError: error,
          menuValidating: isValidating,
          menuEmpty: !isLoading && !data?.length
        };
      }, [data, error, isLoading, isValidating]);
    
      return memoizedValue;
    }

1.  Add a file `**menu.tsx**` in the src/menu-items, and copy the code from `**dashboard.tsx**` (src/menu-items/). Set icons and local files according to the API response.
    
2.  Open the file `**index.tsx**` _(_src/layout/Dashboard/Drawer/DrawerContent/Navigation/index.tsx_)_, and add the code below the line.
    

src/layout/Dashboard/Drawer/DrawerContent/Navigation/index.tsx

Copy

    import { useGetMenu } from 'api/menu';
    import menuItem from 'menu-items';
    import { MenuFromAPI } from 'menu-items/dashboard';
    
    function isFound(arr: any, str: string) {
      return arr.items.some((element: any) => {
        if (element.id === str) {
          return true;
        }
        return false;
      });
    }
    
    // ==============================|| DRAWER CONTENT - NAVIGATION ||============================== //
    
    export default function Navigation() {
      const { menuLoading } = useGetMenu();
      
      const [menuItems, setMenuItems] = useState<{ items: NavItemType[] }>({ items: [] });
    
      const dashboardMenu = MenuFromAPI();
      useLayoutEffect(() => {
        if (menuLoading && !isFound(menuItem, 'group-dashboard-loading')) {
          menuItem.items.splice(0, 0, dashboardMenu);
          setMenuItems({ items: [...menuItem.items] });
        } else if (!menuLoading && dashboardMenu?.id !== undefined && !isFound(menuItem, 'group-dashboard')) {
          menuItem.items.splice(0, 1, dashboardMenu);
          setMenuItems({ items: [...menuItem.items] });
        } else {
          setMenuItems({ items: [...menuItem.items] });
        }
        // eslint-disable-next-line
      }, [menuLoading]);
    
      ...
    }

To add a menu from the backend, you can follow the steps below:

1.  Open the file `**menu.js**` _(src/api/menu.js)_, and edit the API URL in the **useGetMenu** function
    

src/api/menu.js

Copy

    const endpoints = {
      key: 'api/menu',
      dashboard: '/dashboard' // server URL
    };
    
    export function useGetMenu() {
      const { data, isLoading, error, isValidating } = useSWR(endpoints.key + endpoints.dashboard, fetcher, {
        revalidateIfStale: false,
        revalidateOnFocus: false,
        revalidateOnReconnect: false
      });
    
      const memoizedValue = useMemo(() => {
        let updatedMenu = data?.dashboard;
    
        if (updatedMenu && Array.isArray(updatedMenu.children) && updatedMenu.children.length > 0) {
          updatedMenu = {
            ...updatedMenu,
            children: updatedMenu.children.map((group) => {
              if (Array.isArray(group.children)) {
                return {
                  ...group,
                  children: [...group.children, staticMenuItem]
                };
              }
              return group;
            })
          };
        }
    
        return {
          menu: updatedMenu,
          menuLoading: isLoading,
          menuError: error,
          menuValidating: isValidating,
          menuEmpty: !isLoading && !data?.length
        };
      }, [data, error, isLoading, isValidating]);
    
      return memoizedValue;
    }

# Remove Auth | NextJS | Able Pro

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/nextjs/how-to/remove-auth#disable-authentication-temporary)

**Disable Authentication Temporary**


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Disabling authentication temporarily is generally not recommended due to security risks. However, if you have a specific scenario where you need to disable authentication for a short period, here are some steps you can follow:

1.  Comment out the `AuthGuard` wrapper for the routes within the `DashboardLayout` element:
    

NEXT(TS)

NEXT(JS)

src/app/(dashboard)/layout.tsx

Copy

    // project-imports
    import DashboardLayout from 'layout/DashboardLayout';
    // import AuthGuard from 'utils/route-guard/AuthGuard';
    
    // ==============================|| DASHBOARD LAYOUT ||============================== //
    
    export default function Layout({ children }: { children: React.ReactNode }) {
      return (
        // <AuthGuard>
              <DashboardLayout>{children}</DashboardLayout>
        // </AuthGuard>
      );
    }

src/app/(dashboard)/layout.jsx

Copy

    // project-imports
    import DashboardLayout from 'layout/DashboardLayout';
    // import AuthGuard from 'utils/route-guard/AuthGuard';
    
    // ==============================|| DASHBOARD LAYOUT ||============================== //
    
    export default function Layout({ children }) {
      return (
        // <AuthGuard>
              <DashboardLayout>{children}</DashboardLayout>
        // </AuthGuard>
      );
    }

In the code snippet above, the `<AuthGuard>` a component is commented out, allowing the routes within the `DashboardLayout`component to be rendered without authentication protection. To enable the AuthGuard wrapper again, remove the comment markers (`//`) surrounding the `<AuthGuard>` component.

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/nextjs/how-to/remove-auth#remove-authentication-permanent)

Remove Authentication Permanent


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If you want to remove authentication from a system or application permanently, here are the steps to follow:

1.  Remove below authentication keys below from `**next.config.js**` file.
    

next.config.js

Copy

    ...
    .
    NEXT_APP_JWT_SECRET: 
    NEXT_APP_JWT_TIMEOUT: 
    NEXTAUTH_SECRET_KEY: 
    

1.  Removed below list of files and directories.
    

Copy

    ├── src
    │   ├── app       
    │   │   ├── auth (remove directory with all sub files)
    │   │   ├── api (remove directory with all sub files)
    │   ├── views
    │   │   ├── authentication (remove directory with all sub files)
    │   │   ├── auth (remove directory with all sub files)
    │   ├── sections
    │   │   ├── auth (remove directory with all sub files)
    │   ├── utils
    │   │   ├── route-guard (remove directory with all sub files)
    │   │   ├── authOptions.ts

1.  Commented out the full file `**./src/utils/axios.ts**`
    
2.  Remove or change `**/login**` routes.
    
    *   **If you want to remove routes**, remove the router component `Link` with `href=''` props.
        
    *   **If you want to change url**, set the home page URL like, `to={APP_DEFAULT_PATH}` , And import `APP_DEFAULT_PATH` from `config` file.

[NextFigma](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/nextjs/figma)

# Seed | NextJS | Able Pro

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/nextjs/integration/seed#get-started-with-seed)

Get started with Seed


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Seed is the real seed for any new react project. If you think that you know react very well, a seed is a perfect version for you. **Seed is a folder structure created using react-script with minimal files from the full version to get started**. All the unused dependencies are removed from `package.json` unlike the skeleton version, which does not have the same packages as the full version. All the unused files and references were removed, like routes, sections, context, API, data, etc. You can check the difference between skeleton and seed on to next page. The seed version is created for those who just want a theme and then want to implement their own things.

The Seed version is only available after you purchase a theme.

So when you run the project using yarn/npm, you will see a minimal site like below:

![](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FwavVPBvcjnLZ17Y9HyuV%2Fblobs%2FkXhMDC3AuxwBGeBnFk5Q%2Fimage.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=49954725&sv=2)

It provides you with a very simple and intuitive structure to get started with a new project. You can add new components from the full version. Now let's see how we can do that.

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/nextjs/integration/seed#add-components-to-the-skeleton-new-project)

Add components to the skeleton/new project

Now, let's add some cool components from the full version to the project that we just created. It will help you craft your pages as per your needs. So let's begin:

Consider a scenario where you want to add `Total Users` a widget (Left card on the analytics dashboard) from the full version to the sample page. For that, we need to do the following things in order.

1.  Copy the following code and replace it with the sample-page
    
2.  You will see there will be an import error for EcommerceDataCard, so you need to go to full-version, find out component, and copy that component from the full version to the skeleton. That's it.
    

Copy

    
    // material-ui
    import { useTheme } from '@mui/material/styles';
    import { Grid, Typography } from '@mui/material';
    
    // project-import
    import EcommerceDataCard from 'components/cards/statistics/EcommerceDataCard';
    import EcommerceDataChart from './EcommerceDataChart';
    
    // assets
    import { ArrowUp, Wallet3 } from 'iconsax-react';
    
    // ==============================|| SAMPLE PAGE ||============================== //
    
    const SamplePage = () => {
      const theme = useTheme();
    
      return (
        <Grid container>
          <Grid item xs={12} sm={6} lg={3}>
            <EcommerceDataCard
              title="All Earnings"
              count="$3000"
              iconPrimary={<Wallet3 />}
              percentage={
                <Typography color="primary" sx={{ display: 'flex', alignItems: 'center', gap: 0.5 }}>
                  <ArrowUp size={16} style={{ transform: 'rotate(45deg)' }} /> 30.6%
                </Typography>
              }
            >
              <EcommerceDataChart color={theme.palette.primary.main} />
            </EcommerceDataCard>
          </Grid>
        </Grid>
      );
    };
    
    export default SamplePage;

It will output as follows:

![](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fcontent.gitbook.com%2Fcontent%2FwavVPBvcjnLZ17Y9HyuV%2Fblobs%2FbSjrGrlvOVPZz1Zgpn2m%2Fimage.png&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=5020d6e7&sv=2)

Cool and straightforward, right?

You can do the same for other components and design your pages as per your needs. We have made common and reusable controls as well, which you can see inside `/src/components`. Feel free to refer to those as well and start developing your page.

I hope we cover some basics to get started with the Able pro template and how to integrate it for your new project.

[NextComparison](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/nextjs/integration/comparison)

# Documentation | Vue | Able Pro

![](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2439842683-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FVwRshyiG60HEIyPsuxcb%252Fuploads%252F0cCH0Uj4155hX3rBoV4U%252FVuetify%2520Admin%2520Dashboard%2520Template%2520v1.6.0.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Da56e5a96-8d1d-4d31-af23-22dbe222d09d&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=21e3c152&sv=2)

v1.6.0

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/vue/#about-able-pro-vuetify)

About Able Pro Vuetify

Able Pro is a `developer-friendly` & highly customizable Vuejs 3 Admin Template made using [Vuetify](https://vuetifyjs.com/en/)
.

A great deal of familiar Vuetify components is ready to use in Ablepro. These components will help you to build your site faster and save your development time.

We’ve followed the best industry standards to make our product easy, fast & highly scalable to work with. It's made with this high-end technology stack - **Vuetify, Authentication Method - JWT, Vue 3, and pinia.**

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/vue/#technology-stack)

Technology Stack

*   Vuetify v3 components library
    
*   Authentication Method(s) - JWT
    
*   Axios
    
*   Pinia
    

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/vue/#credits)

Credits

*   [Vuetify 3](https://next.vuetifyjs.com/en/)
    
*   [Authentication Method - JWT](https://jwt.io/)
    
*   [Axios](https://axios-http.com/)
    
*   [Pinia](https://pinia.vuejs.org/)
    
*   [Perfect Scrollbar](https://github.com/lecion/vue-perfect-scrollbar#readme)
    
*   [Font Source](https://fontsource.org/)
    

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/vue/#any-suggestion-or-feedback)

Any Suggestion? OR Feedback

 We would love to hear from you anytime.

# Documentation | Vue Laravel | Able Pro

![](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3025910797-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FQ3eW0J6vSeXKIjq75PiA%252Fuploads%252FcZXIhprH2MfKIcLHBPeV%252FVue%2520with%2520Laravel%2520Admin%2520Dashboard%2520Template%2520v1.4.1.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D40eb6cf8-516d-49cc-9389-9217f84927a9&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=d16c60da&sv=2)

Able Pro is a `developer-friendly` & highly customizable **Vuejs 3** with **Laravel 10** Admin Template made using [Vuetify](https://vuetifyjs.com/en/)
.

A great deal of familiar Vuetify components is ready to use in Ablepro. These components will help you to build your site faster and save your development time.

We’ve followed the best industry standards to make our product easy, fast & highly scalable to work with. It's made with this high-end technology stack - **Vuetify, Laravel,Authentication Method - Sanctum, Vue 3, and pinia.**

# Overview | React | Able Pro

![](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2131973819-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FEAF6xFq5HycB0flEqRF4%252Fuploads%252FbB3ad8rZ2u1g9mwdropd%252FReact%2520Admin%2520Dashboard%2520Template%2520-%2520v10.0.0.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D10da9e91-5640-41f6-98a5-60dc1fe8c2e2&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=ea9372de&sv=2)

v10.1.0

**Able Pro React MUI** is a powerful admin dashboard template built with **Material-UI (MUI)**. It offers pre-built components, layouts, and apps, making development faster and easier. Fully customizable and responsive, it's perfect for dashboards, CRM systems, and analytics platforms. 🚀

**Video Tutorial Series**

![](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2131973819-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FEAF6xFq5HycB0flEqRF4%252Fuploads%252Fovf83M8TwfddcySYzUUF%252Fadv-video-tutorial.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D4520cc63-183c-4d04-b51b-d748533af56b&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=29e8697&sv=2)

[Click to Watch the Video Tutorial Series of Able Pro Dashboard Template](https://www.youtube.com/playlist?list=PLiJyhHLaz7pSO99F8BXoXh5Af76raJGK4)

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/react/#technology-stack)

Technology Stack


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   React 19
    
*   Material UI v7 components library
    
*   Authentication Methods - Auth0, Firebase, JWT, AWS
    
*   React Hooks API
    
*   SWR & React Context API for State Management
    
*   React Router v7
    
*   Axios
    
*   Vite
    
*   Code Splitting
    
*   CSS-in-JS
    
*   Multi-Language
    

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/react/#credits)

Credits


------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   [React 19](https://react.dev/blog/2024/12/05/react-19)
    
*   [Material UI v7](https://mui.com/)
    
*   [Vite](https://vitejs.dev/guide/)
    
*   [SWR](https://swr.vercel.app/)
    
*   [React Router](https://github.com/ReactTraining/react-router)
    
*   [Firebase](https://firebase.google.com/docs/auth)
    , [Auth0](https://auth0.com/)
    , [JWT](https://jwt.io/)
    , [AWS Cognito](https://aws.amazon.com/cognito/)
    
*   [Google Fonts](https://fonts.google.com/)

# Quick Start | Bootstrap | Able Pro

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/bootstrap/quick-start#installation)

Installation

Navigate to your root folder **(i.e. ablepro-vanilla-js)**

Copy

    c:>cd able-pro-vanilla-js

Install packages by npm or yarn according to your preferences. Here we are using the npm package manager.

Copy

    > npm i

After package installation, you can start your app by using `**Gulp**` command. This will regenerate the dist folder. You can keep this command running while making changes in the `src` folder. It will auto-apply to the `dist` folder and your browser.

Copy

    > gulp

If you are interested more in learning about gulp, check the below section, else you can skip it.

Gulp[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/bootstrap/quick-start#gulp)

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/bootstrap/quick-start#dont-know-about-gulp)

Don't know about Gulp?

Gulp is a toolkit for automating painful or time-consuming tasks in your project development workflow, so you can stop messing around and build something easier than ever.

*   Auto Minify/Uglify CSS, HTML, and JS codes
    
*   Auto Compile SaSS file
    
*   3000+ Plugins
    

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/bootstrap/quick-start#gulp-for-able-pro)

Gulp for Able pro

Use Gulp in Able Pro for building different layouts and theme customization with lots of functional tasks like Image Optimization, SaSS compilation, etc...which useful to make the production-ready `dist/`directory

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/bootstrap/quick-start#gulp-commands-task)

**Gulp Commands(task)**

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/bootstrap/quick-start#default-task)

Default task

Gulp Command

Description

gulp

which build template in `/dist` directory

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/bootstrap/quick-start#basic-task)

Basic task

Gulp Command

Description

gulp sass

which compile .scss files from `/src/assets/scss` directory and place it into a `/dist/assets/css` directory

gulp imgmin

which use to optimize images from `/src/assets/images` directory and place it into a `/dist/assets/images` directory

gulp build

which use to copy files from `/src/assets` directory and place it into a `/dist/assets` directory

gulp build-html

which uses compiling your HTML file from `/src/html` directory and place it into a `/dist` directory

gulp build-js

which use to build `.js` files from `/src/assets/js` directory and place it into a `/dist/assets/js` directory

gulp watch

It will automatically start your build process if you make any changes in HTML, scss or js files from `/src` directory and put new changes to `/dist` directory

gulp watch-minify

It will automatically start your build process if you make any changes in HTML, scss or js files from `/src` directory and put new changes to `/dist` directory with **minify assets**

[PreviousWelcome](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/bootstrap)
[NextStructure](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/bootstrap/structure)

Last updated 11 months ago

# Quick Start | Tailwind - HTML | Able Pro

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/tailwind-html/quick-start#installation)

Installation

Navigate to your root folder **(i.e. ablepro-tailwind****)**

Copy

    c:>cd able-pro-tailwind

Install packages by npm or yarn according to your preferences. Here we are using the npm package manager.

Copy

    > npm i

After package installation, you can start your app by using `**Gulp**` command. This will regenerate the dist folder. You can keep this command running while making changes in the `src` folder. It will auto-apply to the `dist` folder and your browser.

Copy

    > gulp

If you are interested more in learning about gulp, check the below section, else you can skip it.

Gulp[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/tailwind-html/quick-start#gulp)

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/tailwind-html/quick-start#dont-know-about-gulp)

Don't know about Gulp?

Gulp is a toolkit for automating painful or time-consuming tasks in your project development workflow, so you can stop messing around and build something easier than ever.

*   Auto Minify/Uglify CSS, HTML, and JS codes
    
*   Auto Compile SaSS file
    
*   3000+ Plugins
    

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/tailwind-html/quick-start#gulp-for-able-pro)

Gulp for Able pro

Use Gulp in Able Pro for building different layouts and theme customization with lots of functional tasks like Image Optimization, SaSS compilation, etc...which useful to make the production-ready `dist/`directory

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/tailwind-html/quick-start#dont-know-about-gulp-1)

Don't know about Gulp?

Gulp is a toolkit for automating painful or time-consuming tasks in your project development workflow, so you can stop messing around and build something easier than ever.

*   Auto Minify/Uglify CSS, HTML, and JS codes
    
*   Auto Compile SaSS file
    
*   3000+ Plugins
    

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/tailwind-html/quick-start#gulp-for-able-pro-1)

Gulp for Able pro

Use Gulp in Able pro is for building different layouts and theme customization with lots of functional tasks like Image Optimization, SaSS compilation, etc...which really useful to make the production-ready `dist/`directory

**How to set up Gulp for Able pro?**

1.  Make sure that you have already installed **Nodejs and Gulp** on your server/computer
    
2.  Open the "Nodejs Command prompt" and redirect to your project root directory.
    
3.  Enter the command `yarn` in the command prompt.
    
4.  After that, you must run the below tasks to build a production-ready dist/ directory.
    

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/tailwind-html/quick-start#gulp-commands-task)

**Gulp Commands(task)**

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/tailwind-html/quick-start#default-task)

Default task

Gulp Command

Description

gulp

which build template in `/dist` directory

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/tailwind-html/quick-start#basic-task)

Basic task

Gulp Command

Description

gulp sass

which compile .scss files from `/src/assets/scss` directory and place it into a `/dist/assets/css` directory

gulp imgmin

which use to optimize images from `/src/assets/images` directory and place it into a `/dist/assets/images` directory

gulp build-node-modules

which use to copy files from `/src/assets` directory and place it into a `/dist/assets` directory

gulp build-html

which uses compiling your HTML file from `/src/html` directory and place it into a `/dist` directory

gulp build-js

which use to build `.js` files from `/src/assets/js` directory and place it into a `/dist/assets/js` directory

gulp watch

It will automatically start your build process if you make any changes in HTML, scss or js files from `/src` directory and put new changes to `/dist` directory

gulp watch-minify

It will automatically start your build process if you make any changes in HTML, scss or js files from `/src` directory and put new changes to `/dist` directory with **minify assets**

[PreviousWelcome](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/tailwind-html)
[NextStructure](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/tailwind-html/structure)

# Quick Installation | Angular | Able Pro

You **don’t** need to install or configure tools like WebPack or CLI. They are configured and hidden so that you can focus on the code.

1.  First of all, it's required to Install [Node](https://nodejs.org/en/)
     and npm.
    
2.  Update the latest [angular-cli](https://cli.angular.io/)
     global package to Angular 20+ with CLI 20.x.x
    
3.  Unzip the **able-pro-angular**, and you will find the /project folder.
    
4.  Open the terminal, **install the required node packages** using the following command
    
    Copy
    
        npm install
    
5.  To run the project **locally,** run the following command will run the app in development mode. Open [http://localhost:4200](http://localhost:4200/)
     to view it in the browser.
    
    Copy
    
        npm run start
    
6.  The page will automatically reload if you make changes to the code.
    
7.  Now you can use this Angular project for your application development and make the necessary changes.
    
8.  To build the app for production, the following command will create the `dist/` folder inside this project directory.
    
    Copy
    
        npm run build
    

The project was built assuming it is hosted at the server root folder of the domain/platform i.e`**http://example.com**`

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/angular/quick-installation#or)

or


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------

to deploy build for sub-folder i.e`**http://example.com/folder-name**`

You also need to set **<base href="/folder-name/">**

[PreviousIntroduction](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/angular)
[NextDirectory Structure](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/angular/directory-structure)

# Pre-requisites | Vue | Able Pro

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/vue/pre-requisites#pre-requisites)

**Pre-requisites**

Able-pro vue is based on `nodejs.` Please check the following **prerequisites** before jumping on it.

In your command terminal and check using the `**node -v**` command

Copy

    node -v
    v22.16.0

**Package Manager** - npm or yarn

Copy

    yarn -v
    1.22.22

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/vue/pre-requisites#troubleshooting)

**Troubleshooting**

If you face the following error in your terminal, it means **Yarn** is not installed in your system.

Copy

    yarn -v
    'yarn' is not recognised as an internal or external command,
    operable program or batch file.

Please install it using this [link](https://yarnpkg.com/getting-started/install)
, as it does not come with **Node** automatically.

[PreviousDocumentation](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/vue)
[NextQuick Start](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/vue/quick-start)

# Directory Structure | Angular | Able Pro

Copy

    
    ├── src/
    │   ├── app/
    │   │   ├── @theme/                           -> Theming for the project will be managed here
    │   │   │   ├── components/                   -> Custom-made component of theme
    │   │   │   │   ├── card      
    │   │   │   │   ├── breadcrumb                -> Theme breadcrumb               
    │   │   │   │   ├── helpers
    │   │   │   │   ├── modal-dialog             
    │   │   │   │   ├── navigation/               -> Navigation components
    │   │   │   ├── layouts/                      -> Layout for dashboard
    │   │   │   │   ├── menu/
    │   │   │   │   │   ├── vertical-menu/
    │   │   │   │   │   ├── ...
    │   │   │   │   ├── toolbar/
    │   │   │   ├── service/                      -> Services related to theme
    │   │   │   ├── styles/
    │   │   │   │   ├── layout                    -> Layout scss
    │   │   │   │   ├── pages                     -> Pages scss
    │   │   │   │   ├── theme-mode                -> Theming mode scss   
    │   │   │   │   ├── grid.scss                 -> Gird layout scss  
    │   │   │   │   ├── theme-overrides.scss      -> Angular material overrides
    │   │   │   │   ├── theme-dark-palette-colors.scss      -> Theming dark color scss
    │   │   │   │   ├── theme-palette-colors.scss -> Theming color scss
    │   │   │   │   ├── theme.scss                -> Theming scss
    │   │   │   ├── types/   
    │   │   ├── demo/                
    │   │   │   ├── data/                    
    │   │   │   │   ├── component.ts
    │   │   │   │   ├── menu.ts   
    │   │   │   ├── layout/
    │   │   │   │   ├── admin
    │   │   │   │   ├── component
    │   │   │   │   ├── empty
    │   │   │   │   ├── front
    │   │   │   ├── pages/                        -> View files for all pages
    │   │   │   │   ├── admin-panel/              -> Admin Panel
    │   │   │   │   │   ├── helpdesk/
    │   │   │   │   │   ├── invoice/
    │   │   │   │   │   ├── membership/
    │   │   │   │   │   ├── online-courses/
    │   │   │   │   ├── application/              -> Application pages
    │   │   │   │   │   ├── calender
    │   │   │   │   │   ├── kanban
    │   │   │   │   │   ├── ...
    │   │   │   │   ├── auth/                     -> Auth pages
    │   │   │   │   │   ├── authentication-1/
    │   │   │   │   │   ├── ...
    │   │   │   │   ├── dashboard/                -> Dashboard page
    │   │   │   │   ├── components/               -> Angular material component page
    │   │   │   │   │   ├── data-display/
    │   │   │   │   │   ├── ...
    │   │   │   │   ├── ...                       -> Other theme page
    │   │   │   ├── shared/
    │   │   ├── fake-data/                        -> Dummy data
    │   │   ├── app.component.html
    │   │   ├── app.component.scss
    │   │   ├── app.component.ts
    │   │   ├── app.config.ts                     -> Different theme config
    │   │   ├── app-routing.module.ts             -> Different routes based on layouts
    │   ├── assets/
    │   ├── environments/
    │   ├── SCSS/
    │   │   ├── fonts/
    │   │   ├── more...
    │   ├── style.scss/                           -> Theme style
    │   ├── _index.html
    │   ├── _main.ts
    │   ├── ...
    ├── angular.json                              -> Angular json file
    ├── package.json                              -> Package json file
    ├── ...

# Getting Started | Flask | Able Pro

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/flask/getting-started#prerequisites)

Prerequisites


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/flask/getting-started#code-editor-of-your-choice)

Code Editor of your choice

Before you begin, make sure you have the following installed on your machine:

*   [Node.js](https://nodejs.org/en)
     ( Node v20.\*)
    
*   [Python](https://www.python.org/)
     (3.6 or higher)
    
*   Flask
    

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/flask/getting-started#build-assets)

Build Assets

Before running the application we need to build theme assets:

1.  Open your project to vs code
    
2.  Start a command prompt window or terminal and change directory to Admin/
    
3.  Install packages using one of following commands
    

Copy

    npm install
    
    npm run build

**This command will fetch all dependencies listed in** `**/package.json**` **and place them into**`**/node_modules**` **folde**r.

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/flask/getting-started#install-python)

Install Python

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/flask/getting-started#flask-is-a-python-web-framework.-see-what-python-version-can-i-use-with-flask-for-details)

Flask is a Python web framework. See [What Python version can I use with Flask?](https://flask.palletsprojects.com/en/3.0.x/installation/)
 for details.

1.  Get the latest version of Python at [https://www.python.org/downloads/](https://www.python.org/downloads/)
     or with your operating system’s package manager.
    
2.  Download the executable installer and run it.
    
3.  After installation, open the command prompt and check that the Python version matches the version you installed by executing:
    

Copy

    python --version

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/flask/getting-started#check-pip-version)

Check Pip Version

Copy

    py -m pip --version

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/flask/getting-started#upgrade-pip)

Upgrade Pip

Copy

    py -m pip install --upgrade pip

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/flask/getting-started#virtualenv)

Virtualenv

Make sure to have the `virtualenv` installed globally & running on your computer. You can skip this step if you have already installed it on your computer.

Virtualenv installation command for Linux & mac os

Copy

    python3 -m pip install --user virtualenv

Virtualenv installation command for Windows

Copy

    py -m pip install --user virtualenv

Create a virtual environment for our project. It's always recommended to create separate virtual environments for each project

Copy

    python -m venv environment-name
    
    for mac os
    python3 -m venv environment-name

Activate Virtual Environment on Windows

Copy

    environment-name/Scripts/activate

Activate Virtual Environment on mac OS

Copy

    source ./environment-name/bin/activate

**Note** : Depending on your installation, you may need to use either pip3 or pip and for python you may need to use either python3 or python.

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/flask/getting-started#flask-and-other-dependencies)

Flask And Other Dependencies

Copy

    pip install -r requirements.txt

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/flask/getting-started#run-below-command-for-run-your-project)

Run below command for run your project

Copy

    flask run

[PreviousIntroduction](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/flask)
[NextFolder Structure](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/flask/folder-structure)

# Quick Start | .Net | Able Pro

Able Pro supports ASP.net Core 7. The following is a guide to quickly start using the template.

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/.net/quick-start#prerequisites)

Prerequisites


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/.net/quick-start#visual-studio)

Visual Studio

Make sure to have [Visual Studio](https://visualstudio.microsoft.com/vs/)
 downloaded on your machine. Currently, Able Pro supports ASP.net Core 7 or newer.

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/.net/quick-start#build-theme)

Build Theme

Navigate to your root folder **(i.e. ablepro-dotnet)**

Copy

    c:>cd able-dotnet

Install packages by npm or yarn according to your preferences. Here we are using the npm package manager.

Copy

    > npm i

After package installation, you can start your app by using `**Gulp**` command. This will regenerate the wwwroot/assets folder. You can keep this command running while making changes in the `src` folder. It will auto-apply to the `wwwroot` folder and your browser.

Copy

    > gulp

Go to the root directory of the project and open `**AbleproDotNet.sln**` solution file in Visual studio.

If you are interested more in learning about gulp, check the below section, else you can skip it.

Gulp[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/.net/quick-start#gulp)

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/.net/quick-start#dont-know-about-gulp)

Don't know about Gulp?

Gulp is a toolkit for automating painful or time-consuming tasks in your project development workflow, so you can stop messing around and build something easier than ever.

*   Auto Minify/Uglify CSS, HTML, and JS codes
    
*   Auto Compile SaSS file
    
*   3000+ Plugins
    

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/.net/quick-start#gulp-for-able-pro)

Gulp for Able pro

Use Gulp in Able Pro for building assets for theme with lots of functional tasks like Image Optimization, SaSS compilation, etc...which useful to make the production-ready `wwwroot/assets` directory

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/.net/quick-start#gulp-commands-task)

**Gulp Commands(task)**

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/.net/quick-start#default-task)

Default task

Gulp Command

Description

`gulp`

which build assets in `**wwwroot/**` directory

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/.net/quick-start#basic-task)

Basic task

Gulp Command

Description

`gulp sass`

which compile .scss files from `/src/assets/scss` directory and place it into a `/dist/assets/css` directory

`gulp imgmin`

which use to optimize images from `/src/assets/images` directory and place it into a `/dist/assets/images` directory

`gulp build`

which use to copy files from `/src/assets` directory and place it into a `/dist/assets` directory

`gulp build-html`

which uses compiling your HTML file from `/src/html` directory and place it into a `/dist` directory

`gulp build-js`

which use to build `.js` files from `/src/assets/js` directory and place it into a `/dist/assets/js` directory

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/.net/quick-start#now-compile-and-run-the-project-using-visual-studio)

Now Compile and run the project using visual studio

[PreviousIntroduction](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/.net)
[NextFolder Structure](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/.net/folder-structure)

Last updated 11 months ago

# Getting Started | Django | Able Pro

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/django/getting-started#prerequisites)

Prerequisites


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/django/getting-started#code-editor-of-your-choice)

Code Editor of your choice

Before you begin, make sure you have the following installed on your machine:

*   [Node.js](https://nodejs.org/en)
     ( Node v20.\*)
    
*   [Python](https://www.python.org/)
     (3.6 or higher)
    
*   [Django](https://www.djangoproject.com/)
     (4.2 or higher)
    

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/django/getting-started#build-assets)

Build Assets

Before running the application we need to build theme assets:

1.  Open your project to vs code
    
2.  Start a command prompt window or terminal and change directory to Admin/
    
3.  Install packages using one of following commands
    

Copy

    npm install
    
    npm run build

**This command will fetch all dependencies listed in** `**/package.json**` **and place them into**`**/node_modules**` **folde**r.

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/django/getting-started#install-python)

Install Python

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/django/getting-started#django-is-a-python-web-framework.-see-what-python-version-can-i-use-with-django-for-details)

Django is a Python web framework. See [What Python version can I use with Django?](https://docs.djangoproject.com/en/4.0/faq/install/#faq-python-version-support)
 for details.

1.  Get the latest version of Python at [https://www.python.org/downloads/](https://www.python.org/downloads/)
     or with your operating system’s package manager.
    
2.  Download the executable installer and run it.
    
3.  After installation, open the command prompt and check that the Python version matches the version you installed by executing:
    

Copy

    python --version

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/django/getting-started#check-pip-version)

Check Pip Version

Copy

    py -m pip --version
    upgrade pip
    py -m pip install --upgrade pip

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/django/getting-started#virtualenv)

Virtualenv

Make sure to have the `virtualenv` installed globally & running on your computer. You can skip this step if you have already installed it on your computer.

Virtualenv installation command for Linux & mac os

Copy

    python3 -m pip install --user virtualenv

Virtualenv installation command for Windows

Copy

    py -m pip install --user virtualenv
    or
    py -m pip install virtualenv

Create a virtual environment for our project. It's always recommended to create separate virtual environments for each project

Copy

    python -m venv environment-name
    
    for mac os
    python3 -m venv environment-name

Activate Virtual Environment on Windows

Copy

    environment-name/Scripts/activate

Activate Virtual Environment on mac OS

Copy

    source ./environment-name/bin/activate

**Note** : Depending on your installation, you may need to use either pip3 or pip and for python you may need to use either python3 or python.

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/django/getting-started#django-and-other-dependencies)

Django And Other Dependencies

Install Django on linux & mac OS

Copy

    pip install -r requirements.txt

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/django/getting-started#run-database-migrations)

Run Database migrations

Copy

    python manage.py makemigrations
    
    python manage.py migrate

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/django/getting-started#setting-up-static-files)

Setting up Static Files

Go to Admin/ablepro/settings.py and add following command:-

Copy

    STATIC_URL = 'static/'
    STATICFILES_DIRS = [os.path.join(BASE_DIR,'dist')]

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/django/getting-started#run-below-command-for-run-your-project)

Run below command for run your project

Copy

    python manage.py runserver

# Quick Start | CodeIgnitor | Able Pro

Able Pro supports CodeIgniter 5. The following is a guide to quickly start using the template.

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/code-ignitor/quick-start#prerequisites)

Prerequisites


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/code-ignitor/quick-start#xampp-wamp)

XAMPP/ WAMP

Make sure to have [XAMPP](https://www.apachefriends.org/download.html)
 installed on your computer. Currently, Able Pro supports PHP version 7.4 or newer.

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/code-ignitor/quick-start#composer)

Composer

A composer is a tool for dependency management in PHP. It allows you to declare the libraries your project depends on and it will manage (install/update) them for you.

Make sure to have [Composer](https://getcomposer.org/)
 installed on your computer. Currently, Composer supports PHP version 7.4 to run.

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/code-ignitor/quick-start#installation)

Installation


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Navigate to your root folder **(i.e. ablepro-code-ignitor)**

Copy

    c:>cd able-pro-code-ignitor

Run the following commands step by step.

Copy

    // Install all required packages in the Vendor folder
    
    composer install
    
    // Runs the project
    
    php spark serve

# Quick Start | Vue | Able Pro

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/vue/quick-start#id-1.-package-installation)

1\. Package Installation

Navigate to your project folder.

Copy

    cd able-pro-vuetify-vuejs

Install packages using npm or yarn, as per your preference. Here we are using `**yarn**` the package manager.

Copy

    able-pro-vuetify-vuejs> yarn
    
    or
    
    able-pro-vuetify-vuejs> npm install

**We would recommend yarn over npm**. Why? See this:

[https://www.whitesourcesoftware.com/free-developer-tools/blog/npm-vs-yarn-which-should-you-choose/](https://www.whitesourcesoftware.com/free-developer-tools/blog/npm-vs-yarn-which-should-you-choose/)

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/vue/quick-start#id-2.-start)

2\. Start

Once the package is installed, you can start your app by using `**npm run**` command

Copy

    c:\able-pro-vuetify-vuejs> npm run dev

This will start your local server at `**http://localhost:3000**` Also, the Terminal shows something like this.

Copy

    Compiled successfully!
    
    vite v7.1.4 dev server running at:
    
    > Local: http://localhost:3000/
    > Network: use `--host` to expose
    
    ready in 544ms.

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/vue/quick-start#id-3.-build-and-deploy)

3\. Build & Deploy

To build your app for production use `**yarn build**` command.

Copy

    able-pro-vuetify-vuejs> yarn build
    
    or
    
    able-pro-vuetify-vuejs> npm run build

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/vue/quick-start#id-4.-deploy-for-your-live-site)

4\. Deploy for your live site

Change the base URL with your domain and build your application.

You can control this with the `homepage` field in your `**package.json**`

Copy

    // Package.json
    "homepage": "http://example.com"

**You’ll need to have Node v20.x.x or later on your local development machine** (but it’s not required on the server). You can use [nvm](https://github.com/creationix/nvm#installation)
 (macOS/Linux) or [nvm-windows](https://github.com/coreybutler/nvm-windows#node-version-manager-nvm-for-windows)
 to switch Node versions between different projects easily.

[PreviousPre-requisites](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/vue/pre-requisites)
[NextDirectory Structure](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/vue/directory-structure)

Last updated 1 month ago

# Pre-requisites | React | Able Pro

You don’t need to install or configure tools like Webpack or Babel. They are configured and hidden so that you can focus on the code.

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/react/pre-requisites#pre-requisites)

**Pre-requisites**


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Able Pro is based on `node` and `create-react script`. Please check the following **prerequisites** before jumping on it.

**Node** is the primary prerequisite for Able Pro. Open your command terminal and check using the `**node -v**` command

Copy

    c:\> node -v
    v22.17.1

**Package Manager** - npm

Copy

    c:\> npm -v
    11.5.2

**Package Manager - yarn**

This project uses **Yarn (via Corepack)** for dependency management. The required Yarn version is specified in the `package.json` file, and Corepack ensures the correct version is used automatically. There's no need to install Yarn globally.

**If Corepack is not available:** Corepack is included with Node.js version 16.10+ by default. If it's not installed or enabled:

1.  Ensure you’re using Node.js 16.10 or higher.
    
2.  Enable Corepack by running : `corepack enable`
    
3.  If Corepack is unavailable, update Node.js to a supported version.
    

After Corepack is enabled, simply run `yarn` commands, and the correct version will be handled for you automatically. For more information about Yarn and Corepack, refer to the documentation:

1.  [https://yarnpkg.com/getting-started/install](https://yarnpkg.com/getting-started/installhttps://yarnpkg.com/corepack)
    
2.  [https://yarnpkg.com/corepack](https://yarnpkg.com/getting-started/installhttps://yarnpkg.com/corepack)
    

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/react/pre-requisites#troubleshooting)

**Troubleshooting**


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If you face the following error in your terminal, **npm** is not installed in your system.

Copy

    c:\> npm -v
    'yarn' is not recognized as an internal or external command,
    operable program or batch file.

[PreviousOverview](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/react)
[NextQuick Start](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/react/quick-start)

# Installation | Vue Laravel | Able Pro

**System Requirements / Prerequisites**

*   Node **22.11.0**
    
*   Composer **2.6.6**
    
*   PHP **8.2.12**
    

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/vue-laravel/installation#installation)

Installation

1.  Navigate to your project folder.
    
    Copy
    
        cd able-pro-laravel-vue/full-version
    
2.  Install packages using following two commands.
    
    *   `composer install`
        
    *   `npm install`
        
    
3.  Update `.env` as per your DB setting
    
    Copy
    
        DB_CONNECTION=
        DB_HOST=
        DB_PORT=
        DB_DATABASE=
        DB_USERNAME=
        DB_PASSWORD=
    
4.  Run the following command to **generate the key**.
    
    Copy
    
        php artisan key:generate
    

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/vue-laravel/installation#local-development)

Local development

You can run your **development server** using the dev command. This is useful for local development. The development server **automatically detects** changes to files and instantly displays them in all open browser windows.

Copy

    npm run dev

To serve Laravel, you need to run following command as well in **separate terminal**:

Copy

    php artisan serve

This will run your local server at **http://127.0.0.1:8000** Also, the Terminal shows something like this.

Copy

    
    INFO  Server running on [http://127.0.0.1:8000].
    
    Press Ctrl+C to stop the server

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/vue-laravel/installation#deployment-for-production)

**Deployment for Production**

The assets in your application will be versioned, bundled, and prepared for production deployment when you run the build command:

Copy

    npm run build

[PreviousDocumentation](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/vue-laravel)
[NextDirectory Structure](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/vue-laravel/directory-structure)

Last updated 10 months ago

# Folder Structure | Flask | Able Pro

Copy

    Ablepro Flask
    └─Admin
      ├── 📁src
      |    └── 📁assets
      |        ├── 📁css
      |        ├── 📁fonts
      |        ├── 📁images
      |        ├── 📁js
      |        ├── 📁json
      |        └── 📁scss
      ├── 📁templates
      |      ├── 📄index.html
      |      ├── 📄readme.html
      |      ├── 📁admins
      |      ├── 📁application
      |      ├── 📁chart
      |      ├── 📁dashboard
      |      ├── 📁demo
      |      ├── 📁elements
      |      ├── 📁forms
      |      ├── 📁layouts
      |      ├── 📁other
      |      ├── 📁pages
      |      ├── 📁table
      |      └── 📁widget
      ├── 📄.prettierignore
      ├── 📄 app.py
      ├── 📄db.sqlite3
      ├── 📄package-libs-config.json
      ├── 📄package-lock.json
      ├── 📄package.json
      ├── 📄yarn.lock
      ├── 📄requirements.txt
      └── 📄vite.config.js
    └─Starterkit
      └─ It's easy start with minimal structure of Admin project.
    └─Doc
      └─index.html

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/flask/folder-structure#light-able-django-folders-structure)

Light Able Flask Folders Structure (Root : /Admin)

File/Folder

Path

Description

📁 src/assets

src/assets/

All source file are here.

db.sqlite3

db.sqlite3

All Database related migrations file.

app.py

app.py

Main file for our flask project.

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/flask/folder-structure#light-able-django-templates)

Light Able Flask Templates

File

Path

Description

🗄index.html

templates/index.html

Light Able Preview Page.

📁admins

templates/admins

All application pages are here.

📁 application

templates/application

All application pages are here. Like Account Profile, Chat, eCommerce, Social Media etc.

📁 chart

templates/chart

All chart pages are here.

📁 dashboard

templates/chart

Dashboard page is here.

📁 demo

templates/chart

All the Demo pages here.

📁 elements

templates/elements

All the alerts, buttons, dropdowns, modals etc. elements files are here.

📁 forms

templates/forms

All the forms those are used in our kit are here.

📁 layouts

templates/layouts

All the layout pages like headers, sidebars, customizer and components are here.

📁 other

templates/other

You can all other pages here.

📁 pages

templates/pages

You can all authentication related pages here.

📁 table

templates/table

All tables used in kit are here.

📁 widget

templates/widget

All UI widget pages are here.

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

# Folder Structure | Django | Able Pro

Copy

    Ablepro Django
    └─Admin
      ├── 📁applications
      ├── 📁src
      |    └── 📁assets
      |        ├── 📁css
      |        ├── 📁fonts
      |        ├── 📁images
      |        ├── 📁js
      |        ├── 📁json
      |        └── 📁scss
      ├── 📁ablepro
      |       ├── 📁__pycache__
      |       ├── 📄__init_.py
      |       ├── 📄asgi.py
      |       ├── 📄forms.py
      |       ├── 📄settings.py
      |       ├── 📄urls.py
      |       ├── 📄views.py
      |       └── 📄wsgi.py
      ├── 📁templates
      |      ├── 📄index.html
      |      ├── 📄readme.html
      |      ├── 📁admins
      |      ├── 📁application
      |      ├── 📁chart
      |      ├── 📁dashboard
      |      ├── 📁demo
      |      ├── 📁elements
      |      ├── 📁forms
      |      ├── 📁layouts
      |      ├── 📁other
      |      ├── 📁pages
      |      ├── 📁table
      |      └── 📁widget
      ├── 📄.gitignore
      ├── 📄.prettierignore
      ├── 📄db.sqlite3
      ├── 📄manage.py
      ├── 📄db.sqlite3
      ├── 📄package-libs-config.json
      ├── 📄package-lock.json
      ├── 📄package.json
      ├── 📄yarn.lock
      ├── 📄requirements.txt
      └── 📄README.md
    └─Starterkit
      └─ It's easy start with minimal structure of Admin project.
    └─Doc
      └─index.html

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/django/folder-structure#light-able-django-folders-structure)

Light Able Django Folders Structure (Root: Admin/)

File/Folder

Path

Description

📂ablepro

ablepro

The main app of our project.

📁 src/assets

src/assets/

All source file are here.

db.sqlite3

db.sqlite3

All Database related migrations file.

manage.py

manage.py

Django's command-line utility for administrative tasks.

utils.py

utils.py

All meta data for each page is maintained here.

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/django/folder-structure#light-able-django-templates)

Light Able Django Templates

File

Path

Description

🗄index.html

templates/index.html

Light Able Preview Page.

📁admins

templates/admins

All application pages are here.

📁 application

templates/application

All application pages are here. Like Account Profile, Chat, eCommerce, Social Media etc.

📁 chart

templates/chart

All chart pages are here.

📁 dashboard

templates/chart

Dashboard page is here.

📁 demo

templates/chart

All the Demo pages here.

📁 elements

templates/elements

All the alerts, buttons, dropdowns, modals etc. elements files are here.

📁 forms

templates/forms

All the forms those are used in our kit are here.

📁 layouts

templates/layouts

All the layout pages like headers, sidebars, customizer and components are here.

📁 other

templates/other

You can all other pages here.

📁 pages

templates/pages

You can all authentication related pages here.

📁 table

templates/table

All tables used in kit are here.

📁 widget

templates/widget

All UI widget pages are here.

[PreviousGetting Started](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/django/getting-started)
[Next📄Page Structure](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/django/page-structure)

# Directory Structure | Vue | Able Pro

Under the `**able-pro-vuetify-vue/**` directory, You will find the following folder structure.

Directory Structure

Copy

    able-pro-vuetify-vue
    ..
    
    ├── public
    ├── src
    │   ├── _mockApis                 -> Mock JSON data to be used for apps
    │   ├── assets
    │   │   ├── images
    │   ├── components
    │   ├── layouts
    │   │   ├── blank
    │   │   ├── component
    │   │   ├── dashboard
    │   ├── plugins
    │   │   ├── vuetify.ts            -> Contains theme style and theme
    │   ├── router                    -> Different route based on layouts
    │   ├── SCSS                      -> Theme overrides styles
    │   ├── stores                    -> Getters and Actions
    │   ├── types                     -> Types for TypeScript
    │   ├── utils
    │   │   ├── locales               -> Languages .json files
    │   │   ├── helpers    
    │   ├── views                     -> All Page views
    │   ├── App.vue                   -> Starting point of application
    │   ├── config.ts                 -> Template const value & live customizer
    ├── tsconfig.vite-config.json
    ├── vite.config.ts
    ├── tsconfig.json
    ├── index.html             
    ├── package.json

[PreviousQuick Start](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/vue/quick-start)
[NextTheme UI](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/vue/theme-ui)

Last updated 4 months ago

# Page Structure | Angular | Able Pro

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/angular/page-structure#src-index.html)

.**./src/index.html**

index.html

Copy

    <!doctype html>
    <html lang="en">
      <head>
        <title>Able Pro Angular Dashboard Template</title>
        <base href="/" />
        <!-- Meta -->
        <meta charset="utf-8" />
        <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1, user-scalable=0, minimal-ui" />
        <meta http-equiv="X-UA-Compatible" content="IE=edge" />
        <meta
          name="Able Pro Angular Dashboard Template"
          title="Able Pro Angular Dashboard Template"
          content="Able Pro is a modern Angular dashboard template with a responsive design and powerful features to ease the development process."
        />
        <meta
          name="keywords"
          content="Admin templates, Angular Material Admin templates, angular 20+, Angular Material 20, Dashboard, Dashboard Templates, sass admin templates, html admin templates, Responsive, Angular 20 Admin templates free download, premium Angular 20 Admin templates download"
        />
        <meta name="author" content="PhoenixCoded" />
        <!-- theme style -->
        <link rel="icon" type="image/x-icon" href="favicon.ico" />
        <link rel="preconnect" href="https://fonts.gstatic.com" />
        <link href="https://fonts.googleapis.com/icon?family=Material+Icons" rel="stylesheet" />
        <link rel="stylesheet" href="assets/fonts/inter/inter.css" id="main-font-link" />
      </head>
      <body class="mat-typography">
        <app-root></app-root>
      </body>
    </html>

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/angular/page-structure#src-app-app.component.html)

**../src/app/app.component.html**

app.component.html

Copy

    <router-outlet>
        <!-- loadChildren from app-routing.module.ts with admin.component.html or auth.component.html -->
    </router-outlet>

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/angular/page-structure#src-app-app-routing.module.ts)

**../src/app/app-routing.module.ts**

app-routing.module.ts

Copy

    import { NgModule } from '@angular/core';
    import { RouterModule, Routes } from '@angular/router';
    
    import { AdminComponent } from './demo/layout/admin';
    import { EmptyComponent } from './demo/layout/empty/empty.component';
    import { GuestComponent } from './demo/layout/front/guest.component';
    import { AuthGuardChild } from './@theme/helpers/auth.guard';
    ```
    
    const routes: Routes = [\
     {\
        path: '',\
        component: GuestComponent,\
        children: [\
         // load children modules with lazy load routing for without a common structure, like landing, contact-us, components, etc... \
        ]\
      },\
      {\
        path: '',\
        component: AdminComponent,\
        canActivateChild: [AuthGuardChild],\
        children: [\
          // load children modules with lazy load routing for header, side nav common structure, like, dashboard, blank page, widget, etc...\
        ]\
      },\
      {\
        path: '',\
        component: EmptyComponent,\
        children: [\
         // load children modules with lazy load routing without a common structure, like login, signup, reset the password, maintenance, etc...\
        ]\
      },\
      {\
        path: '**',\
        loadComponent: () => import('./demo/pages/maintenance/error/error.component').then((c) => c.ErrorComponent)\
      }\
    ];

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/angular/page-structure#src-app-demo-layout-admin-admin.component.html)

**../src/app/demo/layout/admin/admin.component.html**

admin.component.html

Copy

    <mat-drawer-container class="example-container" [dir]="direction">
      <mat-drawer #sidebar class="pc-sidebar" [mode]="modeValue" opened>
        <nav>
          <div class="navbar-wrapper">
            <div class="m-header">
              <a>
                <img src="assets/images/logo-dark.svg" />
              </a>
            </div>
            <app-vertical-menu *ngIf="ableProConfig.layout === 'vertical'" [menus]="menus"></app-vertical-menu> <!-- for side nav - vertical.component.html -->
          </div>
        </nav>
      </mat-drawer>
      <app-nav-bar></app-nav-bar>  <!-- for header - toolbar.component.html -->
      <div class="pc-container">
        <div class="coded-wrapper">
          <div class="coded-inner-content">
            <app-breadcrumb [dashboard]="true"></app-breadcrumb> <!-- for common breadcrumb - breadcrumb.component.html -->
            <div class="main-body">
              <div class="page-wrapper">
                <router-outlet>
                <!-- page main body - loadChildren as main page body from src/app/demo/pages/... -->
                </router-outlet>
              </div>
            </div>
          </div>
        </div>
      </div>
      <app-footer></app-footer> <!-- for common footer-->
    </mat-drawer-container>
    <app-configuration></app-configuration> <!-- for common configuration-->

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/angular/page-structure#src-app-demo-layout-empty.component.html)

**../src/app/demo/layout/**empty.component.html

empty.component.html

Copy

    <router-outlet>
        <!-- loadChildren component for guest.component at app-routing.module.ts for authentication blank pages without nav, header, etc. -->
    </router-outlet>

# Directory Structure | Vue Laravel | Able Pro

Under the `**able-pro-vue-laravel/full-version**` directory, You will find the following folder structure.

Directory Structure

Copy

    able-pro-vue-laravel/full-version
    ..
    
    ├── app                          -> Controllers & Models
    ├── bootstrap                    -> Contains cache and app.php
    ├── config                       -> Application's configuration files
    ├── database                     -> Migrations & seeds
    ├── public
    ├── resources
    │   ├── fonts
    │   ├── images
    │   ├── styles                    -> Theme overrides styles
    │   ├── ts
    │   │ 	├── _mockApis          -> Mock JSON data to be used for apps
    │   │ 	├── @core          	-> Common default components auto imports
    │   │ 	├── @layouts          	
    │   │ 	│   ├── components        -> Layouts components
    │   │ 	├── layouts
    │   │  	│   ├── blank
    │   │  	│   ├── component
    │   │  	│   ├── default
    │   │ 	├── pages                 -> All Pages views
    │   │ 	├── plugins
    │   │  	│   ├── fake-api
    │   │  	│   │   ├── handlers      -> Getters and Actions, it's types
    │   │  	│   ├── vuetify           -> Contains theme style and theme
    │   │ 	├── utils
    │   │  	│   ├── i18n          
    │   │  	│   │ 	├── locales       -> Languages .json file
    │   │ 	├── views                 -> All Pages sub components
    │   │  ├── App.vue               -> Starting point of application
    │   ├── views                     -> Laravel setup main file
    ├── routes                        -> Include routes web.php
    ├── storage                       -> Contains compile blade templates
    ├── tests		          -> For testing
    ├── .env  -> Include Database credentials and other environment variables
    ├── eslint.config.js              -> Eslint configuration
    ├── artisan                       -> Include artisan commands 
    ├── auto-imports.d.ts             -> Unplugin auto import file
    ├── components.d.ts               -> Unplugin vue components
    ├── composer.json                 -> Dependencies used by composer
    ├── config.ts                     -> Template const value & live customizer
    ├── env.d.ts                      -> Typescript only(for router layout setup)
    ├── package.json                  -> Dependencies used by node
    ├── tsconfig.json                 -> Typescript configuration
    ├── typed-router.d.ts             -> Unplugin vue router auto import files
    ├── vite.config.ts                -> Laravel's vite file

[PreviousInstallation](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/vue-laravel/installation)
[NextTheme UI](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/vue-laravel/theme-ui)

Last updated 10 months ago

# Getting Started | Nodejs | Able Pro

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/nodejs/getting-started#prerequisites)

Prerequisites


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/nodejs/getting-started#visual-studio)

Visual Studio

Make sure to have [Visual Studio](https://visualstudio.microsoft.com/vs/)
 downloaded on your machine..

Before you begin, make sure you have the following installed on your machine:

1.  [Node.js](https://nodejs.org/)
     Make sure to have [Node.js](https://nodejs.org/)
     installed & running on your computer. If you already have installed Node on your computer, you can skip this step if your existing Node version is greater than 20 or 20. We suggest you to use the LTS version of Node.js.
    
2.  Make sure to have the [NPM](https://www.npmjs.com/)
     installed & running on your computer. If you already have installed NPM on your computer, you can skip this step.
    
3.  A code editor of your choice (e.g., Visual Studio Code, Atom, Sublime Text)
    

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/nodejs/getting-started#build-assets)

Build Assets

Before running the application we need to build theme assets:

1.  Open your project in VS code
    
2.  Start a command prompt window or terminal and change the directory to full-version/
    
3.  Install packages using the following commands
    

Copy

    npm install
    npm run build

Copy

    This command will fetch all dependencies listed in /package.json and place them into/node_modules 
    folder.

#### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/nodejs/getting-started#run-project)

Run Project

To run the Nodejs application navigate your prompt to `project` folder and run the following command. This command will listen for changes and hot reload them.

Copy

    npm run start

Keep your prompt running by default application is served on port [8000](http://localhost:8000/)

Copy

    Enjoy your development with Able-pro 

[PreviousIntroduction](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/nodejs)
[NextFolder Structure](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/nodejs/folder-structure)

Last updated 1 year ago

# 📄Page Structure | Django | Able Pro

Copy

    Django
    
    {% load static %}
    <!doctype html>
    <html lang="en">
        <head>
            {% block title %}
            {% endblock %}
            {% block css1 %}
            {% endblock %}
    
            {% include './head-css.html' %}
            
            {% block css2 %} 
            {% endblock %}
        </head>
    
        <body data-pc-preset="preset-1" data-pc-sidebar-caption="true" data-pc-layout="vertical" data-pc-direction="ltr" data-pc-theme_contrast="" data-pc-theme="light">
        {% include './layout-vertical.html' %} 
        <div class="pc-container">
          <div class="pc-content">
            {% block mainContent %}
            {% endblock %}
          </div>
        </div>
          <!-- Add your main content here -->
          {% include './footer-block.html' %}
          {% include './customizer.html' %}
        
        {% block js1 %}
        {% endblock %}
        {% include './footer-js.html' %}
        {% block js2 %}
        {% endblock %}
      <body>
    
    </html>

### 

[](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/django/page-structure#light-able-django-folders-structure)

Layout settings

You can change the default layout in the templates/index.html file in the body tag

Copy

    
    <body data-pc-preset="preset-1" data-pc-sidebar-caption="true"data-pc-layout="vertical" data-pc-direction="ltr" data-pc-theme_contrast="" data-pc-theme="light">

Attribute

Description

data-pc-preset= "preset-1"

To set the your primary theme color you can change \['preset-1' \] for different color.

data-pc-sidebar-caption= "true"

To set the caption on.

data-pc-layout = "vertical"

To set the vertical Sidebar.

data-pc-direction = "ltr"

To set the layout direction left to right.

data-pc-theme = "light"

To set the layout theme light.

data-pc-theme = "dark"

To set the layout theme dark.

[PreviousFolder Structure](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/django/folder-structure)
[NextCustomizer](https://phoenixcoded.gitbook.io/able-pro/django/customizer)

Last updated 1 year ago
    ```
